Madam Clerk.
COUNTY CLERK: Proceeding with ceremonial resolutions. Members of the public may
testifyin the Council chamber, at courtesy testimony sites,or remotely through the
informationlistedon the meeting agenda.
Individualsinthe Council Chamber may sign up to testifywith the staffmember located
at the desk inthe eighth floorlobby, individualsat courtesy testimony sitesmay sign
up with staffat thatsite.Individualsparticipatingremotely may sign up inthe meeting
chat. Ifyou are connected to the meeting by phone, you willautomaticallybe added
to the testifier list.
Individualsconnected by phone are currentlyon mute and willbe unmuted when itis
theirtime to testify.Individualsconnected by videoconference should keep both their
video and microphones offand should turnthem on only when itistheirtime to testify.
Testimony will be taken before each agenda section, unless extenuating
circumstances require otherwise, subject to approval by a majorityof the Council.
Testimony islimitedto the items listedon the agenda. And individualsmay testifyfor
up to three minutes with one minute to conclude per item. When testifying,please
stateyour name and the name of any organizationyou represent,as well as the items
on which you willbe testifying.Please also identifyto the Council ifyou are a paid
lobbyist.
Individualsmay also be disconnected from the meeting at any time for breaking
decorum. At thistime, individualsmay testifyon ceremonial resolutions.And I'm not
showing any testifiersforthe ceremonial resolutionat thismoment.

Resolution 22-232 about sustainable tourism. As we allknow, we already passed a
sustainable tourism resolution,qualityover quantity.And our committee. I'm speaking
as the Chair of thisDAAC, Climate Action Advisory Committee and as the Chair of the
Sub-Committee on Sustainable Tourism. And we're, we've been working to create and

today.

ones are. And they can apply to multipledomains of sustainable tourism. And thiswill
help us with sustainable tourism quality,inparticular,working on quantitywith the caps
billthat'scoming up and the moratorium, the TIG that'sbeen done. So, allof that is
great stuff.And gettinga commission in place would also be important to actually
implement some certification.So, Ireallysupport thisbill,thisresolution,rather. And
please, please pass itunanimously.
Okay, and I'llturn to the next one, which would be Reso 22-206, eminent domain to
acquire Mauka Ma'alaea property,which I'vespoken on before. Ithinkeminent domain

of allof the.I'm,what Ibelieveare unfairnegotiationsthat have happened concerning
this reallyimportant parcel. And the current owners bought itknowing that itwas
already wanted and was supposed to be bought by the County. So, Idon't reallythink
they'rebeing damaged by eminent domain. And eminent domain, of course, does
provide them fairmarket value.
And so, it'sa process to make itso the County can actuallybe on an equal footingand
negotiate. Because only County negotiation, of course, the public normally is
negotiationsand. . .making itdifficult.So, ifever there was a time, it'snow to use on
thisresolution,on thisparticularpiece of property. So, I really,really,reallysupport
the use of eminent domain foracquiringthisproperty. It'sa reallyimportant property.

ON BEHALF OF COMMITTEE CHAIR GABE JOHNSON, I
MOVE TO ADOPT THE RECOMMENDATIONS IN COMMITTEE
REPORT 22-97.

SECOND.

Discussion? Mr. Molina.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
October?, 2022
Page 53
COUNCILMEMBER MOLINA: Thank you very much, Madam Chair. The Affordable Housing
Committee met on September 1, 6, and 13 of 2022, to discuss the Kuikahi Village
Workforce Housing Projectby developer Alaula Builders.
Under Chapter 2.97, the Council must approve and approve with modificationsor
disapprove the proposed projectwithin60 days afterprojectsubmittal. The 60-day
deadline is Friday, October 14, so today is our opportunity to pass thisprojectwith
modifications.
The Projectis located on 14.97 acres in Wailuku. Itwillconsistof 202 multi-family,
duplex, townhome, live-work,studio,and single-familyunits.The unitswillbe offered
for sale to income-qualifiedhouseholds earning between 51 and 140 percent Area
Median Income.
Your Committee discussed exemptions relatedto land use and zoning, construction
and design standards,and fasttrackpermitting.
Your Committee also discussed concerns relatingto Wailuku Water Reservoir #10,
which borders the Project'ssiteto the north. The Reservoir receiveda Notice of
Deficiencyfrom DLNR inSeptember of 2021.
The Developer agreed to work with Corporation Counsel on an indemnification
agreement to ensure the Reservoir isingood standing beforeany unitsare occupied.
Your Committee also considered various modifications to the project, including
restrictinganimals for wildlifepreservation,requiringunitsto be owner-occupied in
perpetuity,and givingpreferences to long-term residentsof the County.
Your Committee also noted that Bill127 (2022) accompanied the Projectapplication
and proposed changing the State Land Use Designationfrom AgriculturalDistrictto
Urban District,so thatthe projectmay proceed.
Committee agreed thatas a land use ordinance. Bill127 would have togo tothe Maui
Planning Commission under Maui County Charter. The billwas referredto the
planningcommission via Resolution22-217 atthe September 27 Council meeting.
And in the end, your Committee voted 9-0 to recommend adoption of
Resolution 22-193, CD1, approving the projectwith modificationsand the filingof
Resolutions 22-192 and 22-194. 1 respectfullyrequest the Members support of this
motion. Thank you.

COUNCILMEMBER MOLINA: Thank you very much. Madam Chair. And Members, please
bear with me, I might be a littlebitmore long-winded than usual. Your GREAT
Committee met on November 16, 2021, November 24, 2021, January 18, 2022,
March 15 and March 22 of 2022, June 14, 2022, and August 16, 2022, and
September 8, 2022, to discuss legislationto address bicycletour publicsafetyand
relatedlitigationconcerns.
The Committee initiallydiscussed County Communication 21-453, under which I
transmitted a proposed resolutionentitled"URGING THE MAYOR TO ADDRESS
BICYCLE TOUR PUBLIC SAFETY AND RELATED LITIGATION CONCERNS". The
purpose of the proposed resolutionisto urge the Mayor to address bicycle-tourpublic
safety and relatedlitigationconcerns on Maui Island.
Given the weight of the matter, I feltmore stringentaction should be taken and
introduced a billto amend Chapter 5.22, Maui County Code, to establishlimitsand
restrictionsfor commercial bike-tour businesses, and to address publicsafety,traffic,
illegalparking,and relatedlitigationconcerns on Maui Island.
The. as displayed by the long listof meeting dates inwhich 1,we met on thisitem,our
Committee discussed a proposed billand introduced revisionsalong the way, as we,
what was incorporated were revisions based on feedback received and discussions
with the Kula Community Association and bike-tourcompanies who are impacted by
the bill.And by the way, Ido want to thank the Kula Community Associationfortheir
contributionsto this,as well as Councilmember Sugimura.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
October 7, 2022
Page 64
Your Committee received oraland writtentestimony in support of addressing bike-tour
publicsafety and relatedlitigationconcerns, as well as inputfrom CorporationCounsel,
Finance, Parks and Recreation, Planning, Police,Prosecuting Attorney, and Public
Works; ailwho supported the intentof the billand provided feedback on ways to
strengthen the bill’slanguage and address respectiveconcerns relatingtothisindustry.
Representatives from the commercial bike-tour operations expressed concern that
regulationsimposed on guided commercial bike tours could decrease clienteleand
also increasethe number ofvisitorsbikingon busy or dangerous roads withouta guide
or visitorsbikingwith illegaland unpermitted businesses.
Chapter 5.22.020 of our Maui County Code, already prohibitsbusinesses or persons
from conducting commercial bike tours on County and State propertieswithoutfirst
obtaininga bike-tourbusiness permit in accordance with Chapter 5.22,inadditionto
any other requirement of State law.
To furtheraddress these concerns, your Committee added additionalrequirements for
businesses or individualsapplying for a permit and added stricterpenaltiesfor any
person who violatesthe requirements and prohibitionsinexistingsectionsofthe Code.
Your Committee also amended the proposed billby adding the specificationsfor
commercial bike tours operating in the Makawao-Pukalani-Kula and Pa'ia-Ha'iku
Community Plan areas, such as restrictingbike tours to operate only from sunriseto
sunset on Haleakala Crater Road and between specificmile markers, and adding
restrictionsto days and times commercial bike tours can operate on Baldwin Avenue.
The amendments ensure bicyclistsare ridingduring daylightand in areas with less
traffic,increases awareness and respect for culturallysignificantholidays, and
decreases the opportunity for trafficaccidents and backups because bicyclistswould
be ridingoutside peak school and work traffichours.
Your Committee also extended the ordinance effective date to provide ample time for
bike-touroperators to have properlycomply with the bill.
And the, in addition,the all in all,your Committee’s prioritywas the safety and
well-beingof Maui County residentsand visitorswhen addressingconcerns from both
bike-tourcompanies and testifiersrequesting stricterlaws on biketoursand bike-tour
companies.
Your Committee voted 9-0 to recommend passage of thisbillon firstreading and filing
of County Communication 21-453. Mahalo foryour indulgence.Madam Chair,and
also Members. I need a drink of water here after this. Thank you.

Your Committee noted that the purpose of the resolutionis to accept dedication of

Your Committee noted that Resolution 22-208 must be approved in conjunction with

Your Committee noted that as a result of further discussion with A & B, a portionof the
Lot A-1 (Baby Beach), willbe donated to the Maui Country Club as an exclusive
easement. And the remaining 23 acres willbe dedicated to the County and placed in
a land trust. The subdivision of the property is in accordance with
Section 18.04.020(G),Maui County Code.
A representativefrom A & B stated thatthey do not support residentialdevelopment
on the acreage being donated to the Maui Country Club.
The Planning Directorclarifiedthatthisacreage issplitzoned, halfofwhich iszoned
Residential, and the other half zoned Interim. Development on the property would
require a Special Management Area permit, ifexemptions are allowed,that are
consistentwith zoning and community plan area.
A representativefrom the Universityof Hawaii Sea GrantCollegeProgram explained
the importance of keeping the propertyas a naturalbuffertoprotectinfrastructurefrom
coastal hazards.
The Committee also noted that Baby Beach is designated Open Space/Park as
identified in the Maui Island Plan.
The Director of Parks and Recreation explained that the County currentlymanages
and maintains Baldwin Beach Park, Rainbow Park, and Ho’aloha Park through a lease
with A & B. The remaining donated parks not currentlymanaged or maintainedby the
County willstillneed to be assessed and budget,and a budgetamendment toaddress
maintenance costs forthese parks would also be needed.
Your Committee agreed to discharge the Infrastructureand TransportationCommittee
from further consideration of Resolution 22-208 with the understanding that the
Administration would transmit a revised resolution incorporatingrevisionsto Lot A-1,
incorporating,includinga new map and propertydescription.

MR. PAUL TONNESSEN (testifying on Resolution No. 22-228):
My name is Paul Tonnessen and I'm the Executive Directorfor the Friends of the
Children'sJusticeCenter. And today I'm hereto speak on behalfof Resolution22-228.
Assistingsurvivorsof sexual violenceisemotionallydrainingand demanding work that
comes with a personal cost forserviceproviders,especiallythe sexual assaultnursing
examiners also known as SANE nurses.
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
October 7, 2022
Page 84
Personally,as a long-timeadvocate forchildrenwho have been victimizednot only by
sexual abuse, but also physical and emotional abuse, Iknow alltoo wellthe emotional
tollknown as secondary trauma stressor forshort,STS, has had on me. There are
days 1justsitinmy officeand cry due to some of the horrificthings thatare happening
to our keiki on Maui that I have to encounter, and iam not one of the firstresponders.
STS isfound in those who hear about or have to respond to another's trauma rather
than being the victimsthemselves. Secondary trauma has been well-documented in
those who work with sexual assaultsurvivors,especiallythe SANE nurses thatare on
the frontlinesdirectlyresponding afterthe assaulthas taken place.
Numerous studies have found that allthe nurses who care for rape victims reported a
heightened awareness of theirown vulnerability.Half of them reportedchanges in
theirown dailybehaviors. Inthese studies,they'vealso found the SANE nurses have
a variety of emotional responses including anger, nightmares, fear, sadness,
helplessness,anxiety,and difficultyfocusing.
STS creates a high riskof burnout inour human serviceprovidersnationwide. These
burnouts can consistof emotional exhaustion, depersonalization,and a reduced sense
of personal accomplishment. In comparing burnout across varioustypes of nurses,
the highest rates of burnout have been found in the emergency rooms and SANE
nurses compared to nurses who are working withotherpopulationsintheirprofessions.
This job takes a specialperson to do itand the majorityofpeople would not onlybe,
not only,not be able to do it,but would not choose to do it.There are alsorewarding
partsofthistype ofwork inknowing thatby being thereforsomeone aftera traumatic
event has happened to them, they become a safetynet forthem, a sense of security
maybe forthe firsttime ever inthe child'slife.And you are able to be partofa much-
needed healingprocess forthese individuals.
1have watched the SANE staffon Maui forover ten years put aside the stresses ofthe
job and respond to each and every childthey encounter withdignity,empathy and
compassion. When Icome to speak, 1always research what I'mtalkingabout. And
what I found was that the average SANE nurse stays in the profession 1-2 years.
Jennifer,who isone of them, isgoing on ten years now. So, ifthese individualsare
bringingvalue to our community, which they are,then itshouldnotbe difficultforus to
show them that we see the value in them. Most people doing thiswork don'texpect
ridiculousraises or bonuses. They justwant to be paid what they are worth. And by
not doing so,what message willwe be sending to them?
So, Iam humbly asking the Council,while reviewing22-228,to notonlysee the human
value these individuals have for the victims, their families,and our community overall,
Regular Meeting ofthe Council ofthe County of Maui
October?, 2022
Page 85
but to also understand that we need to be in line with other governmental agencies in
providinga faircompensation forour SANE nurses thatthey so rightfullydeserve.
Ijustwant to add one quick thing,because Ididn'tuse up allmy time. These, these
front-lineworkers have a horrificjob. And I'lltellya, they reach out to the community
to make the environment the childcomes into,they callme up and say can you bring
stuffedanimals? Can we have extra clothes,you know? I mean, they go above and
beyond. So, I greatly appreciate it ifyou would consider the increase in their
compensation. Thank you.

woman. Idon't understand at thispointwhy any male nominee would be considered
at thistime. Itseems obvious to me that once one gender has reached fivemembers,

Frampton, and to hold the Department of Water Supply staffaccountable.

Public Trust, as well as Native Hawaiian Law. She's a graduate of the William S.
Richardson School of Law, with certificatesinenvironmental and Native Hawaiian law.

Native Hawaiian Law.

factualand legal research and other support on a range of issues includingNative
Hawaiian traditionaland customary practices,initiativesand policiesimpactingaccess
to freshwater,and water leases under HRS Chapter 171". Just lastyear,she co-taught
an emerging Hawaii water law issues classwith Kapua Sproat.

fiduciaryobligationsand understand and abide by the laws thatgovern itsoperations

paper. But.you know, Icertainlysupport better,betterconditionsforour localworkers.
And Ijustwanted to say that since 19, since the 1990's,when Iserved on the State
Board of Education, we were being toldback then, as the paper was startingto shrink,
but the best way to get an articleinthe paper isto write ityourself. And Iwent to a
workshop and that'swhat we were told. So, we have not had reallya lotof good
investigativereporting,and we need to get back to that local,so thatthe articlescome
from the writerson the Maui News and not from, you know, contributorswho have a
certainpointof view.
But thishas been, that'swhy Iask thatquestion. This isa longstanding problem with
our localpaper since,and itgot worse when itwas purchased by a mainland operation.
So, Idon't know what the answer is.And I,you know. Ithinkthatwas a question that
Member Kama was tryingto get to. But.you know. I'ma big fan of locallyowned local
papers as well. So, Ijustwanted to point out thatthat may be the crux of the problem

Discussion, Vice-Chair Rawlins-Fernandez.
VICE-CHAIR RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ: Mahalo, Chair. Members, the purpose of thisbillis
to amend the FiscalYear 2023 Budget, Appendix A, Part I,to add a new grant under
Department of Housing and Human Concerns, entitled"HOME American Rescue Plan
(HOME-ARP) Program", in the amount of $1,977,568. 30,000 is allowed for
Administrative costs.
The grant funds willbe used for eligiblehousing projectsbased on evaluations of
projectsbeing done to determine which developer would get these HOME-ARP funds.
The funds can only be used for unitsthat would serve households at a lower area
median income.
We do have representativesfrom the Administrationthat are availableto answer
questions. And Idid receive some questions about the use of the funds and got some
information from the Director that the State HHFDC isthe agency thatispass through
for these Federal funds. HHFDC writes the allocationplan for allthe sisterislands.
Based on an amendment to the plan by HHFDC, our County is tied intothe uses
identifiedby the State plan.
HHFDC plan limitsHOME AARP, or ARP, sorry, program funds to acquisition,
production,or rehabilitationofaffordablehousing. The plan also requiresa competitive
process such as an RFP. And unfortunately,the County does not have the optionto

RE: Resolution 22-206
Aloha CouncilChairperson Lee and Maui County CouncilMembers,
Please support Resolution22-206 authorizingproceedings in eminent domain for the
acquisitionof the Ma’alaea Mauka/Pohakea Watershed which received unanimous
approval lastmonth by the CARES Committee.
Itis unfortunate that the new owner of these lands isunwillingto sellthe 257 acre parcel
to the County. Apparently he may be willingto sellor donate a small portion ofthe land
to address erosion and other issues, but keep the remainder in the hopes that he may
receivesupportfordevelopingthe remaining land.The community and thisCouncil has
alreadybeen down thatroutewiththe previousowner and determined the entireparcel
was worth preservingforfuturegenerations.Not onlyfor itsvaluable scenic views and
vistasbutto address wildfireand sedimentationimpacts on Maalaea Bay. The Pohakea
Stormwater Management Plan says the entireparcelisneeded to address these impacts.
Let’sreview:The parcel-projectdistrict12 - isoutside of the Urban Growth Boundary in
the Maui IslandPlan. Hence, only 21 ag. lotsare permittedon the land. The developer
may dangle the hopes of ‘affordablehousing’on the parcel but thatisunrealistic- the
previous owner knew that and was willingto sellthe land to the county. And there are
1400 unitscoming up inWaikapu Country Town and more planned forthe Maalaea to
Wailuku corridor.
With DLNR State Forestrywillingto take ownership and management responsibilityfor
the parcel to combine with the surrounding 4,000 acres of state conservation lands to
createa ‘forestreserve’,it’sa win-winforthe County and forthe Maui community. This
initiativewillprovideMaui County vast resources in preservingthe valuable open space
and scenicresources,expand the historicLahaina PaliTrailand create parks and trails
forthe benefitof Maui’speople foryears to come. DLNR’s commitment of $1 millionin
Legacy Lands fundingtoward the purchase demonstrates the value the state puts on
preserving these lands.
Please support Resolution 22-206 and move thisresolutionfonward withoutfurtherdelay.
Mahalo!
Sincerely,withAloha,
Lynn Britton

Aloha Chair Lee, Vice-Chair Rawlins-Femandez and Members of theCounty Council,
Mahalo forthisopportunitytoprovidetestimonyinadvance oftheCouncil’sOctober7,2022
meeting.TheHawaiiHotelAlliance(HHA)‘ stronglyopposes—inclusiveofrecent
amendments—Bill 21. Bill21 would stillforcea predominance of theMaui community to
undertakeonerousand expensivelightingmeasuresthathave notbeen shown toincreasewildlife
safetybutcouldhave potentialdetrimenttohuman safety.HHA had hoped—^upon Bill2Ts
return to fullCouncil for renewed consideration—that trulysubstantivechanges would have
been made at committee level.
Insteadoffullyrecountingour ongoing trepidationsword-for-word, we encourage all
councilmembers to review our priortestimony and to stronglyoppose Bill21 CD2 FD2.
Maui’slodgingindustryremainsdeeplycommittedtoitsstewardshiprolefortheenvironment,
butthe approachsoughtherewillinvolvetremendous coststoMaui’s government (i.e.,
taxpayers)and businesses,aswellasfraughtabilityto obtainand determinecompliantlighting
mechanisms—all forbluelightstandardslackingscientificconsensus.^Critically,theCouncU
would be establishingseriouslightingstandard burdens that are not broadly substantiated
as having demonstrable benefitsfor Hawaii’s nativeseabirdspeciesand other local
wildlife.^
Where Bill21 CD2 FD2 deviatesmost from priorversionsisinitsexpanded listofexemptions.

remissifwe didnothighlightthatthestandardswould applyto "[tjemporaryhoteland

community and Hawaii's nativewildlife.

storm petrels,and Newell'sshearwatersastheynavigatebetween theoc ianand nesting
colonies,resultinginfallout,injury,and death.Stateand federalwildlifeagencieschargedwith

an ongoingthreattothespecies'survivaland recovery.Bestpracticestommimize light
attraction,and helppreventextinction,includereducingshortwaveleng h "bluelight"in

BILL 21 SEEKING LIMITING OUTDOOR LIGHTING
OFFiCE OF THE
*:OUNTY CLERKTo:

You don'toftengetemailfromjosh@desilvadmccom.Learnwhv thisisimportant
Aloha,
Iam writingto encourage reconsiderationof Bill21 intended to limitoutdoor lightingat events on hoteland
resort properties. Further discussion,clarificationand testimony isrequiredbefore passinga billof this
nature. Luau, corporate group events,fundraisers,weddings and otherspecialevents areconsistentlyheld
outdoors here inHawaii. Restrictingor eliminatingoutdoor lightingatthesetypesofevents poses safety
concerns as wellas potentiallysevere negativeeconomic consequences fora significantnumber of
hardworking locallyowned smallbusinessand not justlargehotels.The rippleeffectsof thisbill,whether
intended or not willbe significantand must be furtherreviewed before finalpassage.
We understandthe need to protectour treasuredwildlife,includingour seabirdsand turtles.Limiting
temporary outdoor events when there has been no proven nexus to the lossof wildlifedoes not make for
good legislation.We stand readyto work withthe Maul County Counciland the County government to
identifyalternativelegislationthatstrikesa betterbalance and protectsour wildlifeand our friendsinthe
event Industry.
Thisbillwould essentiallyprohibitany and alloutdoor up lightingat hotelvenues designedto be used forevening events
and would requireallother lightingfixturesto be properly"shielded"to eliminatelightspillagebeyond the horlzonal
plane of the lightsource.Unlikeother Industries,theatricallightingmanufacturers do not offerany environmentally
friendlyremedialsolutionsor retrofitapparatusthatwould bringlightingfixturesintocompliance.ThisBillis
tantamount to an outrightban on theatricallightingat alloutdoor eveningeventsat resortsand hotels.Meetingand
event plannersoftenselectHawaiias theirpreferreddestinationon the basisofour amazing weather,which allowsfor
outdoor events year-round. Ifenacted intolaw,thisBillwillhave far-reachingconsequences beyond justthe abilityto
lightan event space.Without outdoor lighting,there willbe no outdoor events,and withoutoutdoor events,therewill
be no group or destinationwedding businessresultinginvery realeconomic loss.Maui needs to keep our hospitality
industrystrongso thatworkers can put food on the table,pay rent/mortgage,utilitiesand allthe costsassociatedwith
livingon Maui.
The Billcarvesout narrow exceptionsto these restrictionsthatflyinthe faceofthe expressedpurpose ofthisbill.The
exceptionsincludenighttimesportingevents and other permittedspecialevents{likethe Obon Festival),and eventson
non-profitproperties(e.g.concerts at the MACC) and on County,Stateor Federalproperties(e.g.the annual Barrio
Fiesta,the Maui Fair,etc.),but not forevents athotelsor otherocean-sideeventvenues. Clearly,hotelsare being
targetedwhen these other "permissible”events produce substantiallymore artificialatmosphericlightthan private
resortevents do. Compare the brightwhite glaringlightsatthe War Memorial Stadium sportingevent vs mood lighting
at a hotel outdoor venue.
Clearlythe Bill'sauthor,councilmember KellyKing,and her supportersare unaware of,or unconcerned with,the special
events industry,and are eithermisguided about,or simplywish to ignore,the devastatingimpact thisdraconianoutdoor
lightingban would have on tourism,the resorts,and the specialevents industry.Pleasereconsiderthe passageofthis
billuntilwe can have a fairand proper discussionof itspotentialimpacts.

September 29, 2022
Testimony: Council Meeting set for October 7,2022
Use of roads by automobiles, motorcycles and bicyclescan be hazardous especiallyto bicycleriders
because of bicyclespeed limitationand instabilityformaneuvering withintraffic.
'Canautomobiles,motorcyclesand bicyclescontinueto share thesame road?
Sharingthe road has always been a concern forthe safetyof bicycleridersbut we have accepted this
risk because there has been no viable alternative and the number of accidentsexperienced was
"tolerable".Now that roads are much improved (smoother rideand higher speeds),carsare much
improved (smoother ride,betterstabilityand higherspeeds),and bicyclesare much improved (better
stabilityand ableto achieve higherspeeds only limitedby a rider'sskilland physicalability)we are faced
again with the question:
'Canautomobiles,motorcyclesand bicyclescontinueto share the same road?
The answer is"No". Some communities acknowledge thisby creatingbike lanesto ensure minimum
separationbetween human powered vehicles(bicycles),and gas and electricpowered vehicles(mainly
cars).Thiswas not done justto Influenceincreaseduse of bicyclesbut also presumes that bike lanes are
inherentlysaferespeciallyforthe bicyclerider.However, when bikelanesdo not/cannot exist(ex:
Baldwin Ave, Omaopio Rd and Old Haleakala Highway), allowinguse of bicycleson hillycurvingcountry
roads that lack distance between bikes and cars increases accidentriskbecause of higher speeds riding
downhill as well as unstable maneuvering going up or down hill.
The negativeimpact to businesses(limitingor prohibitingbike touring)isnot at issue.The concern is
simplywhether the councilwillaccept the number of accidents(and deaths)thatoccur each year
compared to accident mitigationmeasures.
Recommendations
Prohibithuman powered vehicles(bicycles)on allroads with no bike lanesand the legalspeed
limitisgreater than 35 MPH.
Limituse of human powered vehicleson ailroads with a grade of 15% or higher.Allow use when
trafficflow islow and the potentialaccidentrateisatan "acceptablerisklevel".
Allow use of human powered vehicleson roads with bike lanesand the legalspeed limitIsequal
to or less than 35 MPH.
Consider the demographics of bicycleaccidents.Are accidentscaused by whom, what, where,
when, why, how? Adjustmitigationeffortsaccordingly.
Educate bike ridersto the following:
a. Understand risks,
b. Share responsibilityforroad safety."Share the road" appliesto bikes,too. Ride single
hie.Move over to allow biggerand fastervehiclesthrough (same courtesy as highways),
c. Take precaution.As Maui driverstend to favortrucksand SUVs, these biggermore
robust vehiclesincreaseroad danger.
1.
2.
3.
4.
5.
September 29,2022
d. Know views may be obstructed.Narrow country roads can have blindcurvesas wellas
vegetation growth,
e. Be extracarefulnavigatingunfamiliarroads.
6. Require bike touringbusinessesthat use publicroads forprofithave a standard customer
orientationemphasizing cautions,bikesafetyand road courtesy.
Clarence and Lenora Dun

RE: Testimony of Hawaii Hotel Alliancein Opposition to Bill21, CDl, FDl (2022)
Aloha ChairLee,Vice-ChairRawiins-Femandez and Members of theCounty Council,
Mahalo forthisopportunitytoprovidetestimonyon behalfofHawaiM HotelAllianceregardingthe
proposedchangestooutdoorlightingrequirements.Bill21,CDl, FDl (2022).Maui’s lodgingindustryis
steadfastlycommittedtoprotectingendangerednativeseabirds,includingby minimizinglighting.
However, forthereasonswe willexpand upon below.Bill21 remainsdeeplyflawed,and we must
regretfullyopposethemeasure.
Bill 21. CDl. FDl Arbitrarily Singles Out Outdoor Events Held at Hotels
As amended,thebillwould impose a seriesofvague and expansivenew rulesfortemporarylightingat
outdoorevents,butforreasonstheproponentsoftheamendment failedtoexplain,itwould onlyapplyto
events at hotels and visitor accommodations.
Saidanotherway, theCouncilwants toholdhotelstoa standardthatitisunwillingtoimpose atfacilities
owned and operatedby Maui County.

APPENDIX E:GuidelinesforAdjustingLightingat Facilities
1. GuidelinesforAdjustingLightingat Facilities
Thisappendixprovidesdetailedguidelinesto informminimization measures that can be
customized to address an arrayofpossiblelightingissuesat Participantfacilities.A lighting
minimizationplan to achieve the maximum extent practicablewillbe included in each
ParticipantPIP.
These guidelinesrepresentbest availablescienceatthe time of KSHCP permit issuance.Over
the lifethe plan,likelynew Informationand new technologieswillbe available,and this
appendix may be updated accordingly.
Not alllightingguidelinesare appropriateforalltypes of facilities.Some represent long term,
infrastructuresolutions,and othersmay be implemented on a seasonal basis.
1.1.Deactivate Non>EssentialLights
Prioritizationof seabirdand honu lightattractionminimizationmeasures Involvesevaluating
lightneeds to determine ifnon-essentiallightscan be deactivatedduringthe seabirdfallout
season (September 15 to December 15) and turtlenestingseason (May 15-December 15).
Deactivatingthe lightsavoidsthe potentialforlightattractionthatthose lightscouldotherwise
cause. Turningoffa subsetof lights,both unshieldedand shielded,during the falloutseason
(September 15 to December 15) can assistwith minimizingthe riskofseabirdlightattraction,if
those lightsare not necessary.IntheirPIPs,Applicantsmust providerationaleforany facility
lightsthatcannot be deactivatedduringseabirdfalloutseason,and detailwhat other
minimizationpracticeswillbe implemented on lightsthatwillremain illuminated.The
regulatoryagencieswillreview the evaluationand justificationas provided inapplicantPIPs.
Similarly,turningout lightsthatshinedirectlyon beaches duringthe turtlenestingseason (May
15-December 15) can prevent hatchlingdisorientation.Avoid use of the followinglamp styles
on beachsideorshoreperpendicularto sidesofa structure:privatebalconylights,up lights;
decorativelighting,not necessaryforhuman safetyor security;pond lights;and beach lighting.
Timers or other similar devices should be used to ensure the selectedlightsremain offduring
the turtlenestingseason. This measure may requirethe installationof independent light
switches. Conversely,to prevent accidentalactivation,lightfixturescan be removed forlights
thatwillno longerbe needed at a facility.
1.2.InstallFullCut-offLightFixtures
A fullcut-offfixturerefersto a lightfixturewhich thatdoes not shinelightabove a 90 degree
horizontalplane. For lightsnecessaryto be activated,fullcut-offfixturesprovidean effective
measure to achieve lightminimizationbecause they prevent lightfrom shiningdirectlyupward.
These types of lightshouse the lightbulb up withinthe fixtureso that no bulb protrudes below
(Figure1). Such fixturesmust be mounted at appropriateangle so they pointdirectlydown to
the ground. Many lightmanufacturers provide lightfixtureinformationalong with the light
specificationsto indicateifa fixtureisa fullcut-offdesign. The InternationalDark Sky
Association(www.darksky.org) isa good source forInformationon fullcut-offlightsand
providesadditionalreferencesto lightengineeringresourcesand lightmanufactures.
Figure1: Examples of fullcut-offlightfixtures.Source: www.darkskv.org.
Along shorelines,exteriorfixtureson the seaward (makai) and the shore perpendicularsidesof
the building(and on the landward sideof the buildingifthey are visiblefrom the beach) should
be down-litfixtures,fullyshieldedand fullcut-off,louvered, or recessed fixturesthat do not
have reflective inner surfaces. These fixtures should use low wattage bulbs(e.g.,<50w). All
exteriorfixtureson the landward (mauka) sideof the buildingshould be directeddownward
only (Witherington& Martin 2003).
1.3.ShieldingLightFixtures
This minimization measure aims to achieve the functional equivalentof a fullcut-offlight
fixtureby installinga shield,visor,hood or similaron an existinglightfixtureto prevent light
from shiningupward and reducing trespass.In additionto the shielding,to achievethe
functionalequivalentof a fullcut-offfixture,a lightfixtureshould be adjustedso thatitpoints
directlydown perpendicular to the ground to create a level,horizontalplane between the
fixtureand the ground, and have the bulb housed within the lightfixture(Figures2 & 3). Reed
et al.(1985) suggest that Inareas where other lightsources are rare,the shieldingof principal
lightswould likelyhave a largereffectin decreasingseabird lightattraction.
I
Figure 2: Installationof an appropriatelysized floodlightshield.Source: www.darkskv.org.

1.4.Angle LightsDownward
Angling and repositioninglightspresents a potentialalternativeto shieldingor replacinglight
fixturesand may be sufficientto make lightsfullycut-offand eliminatelightshininghorizontally
and vertically(Figure4). To achieve the functionalequivalent of a fullcut-offfixture,a light
fixtureshould be adjusted so that itpointsdirectlydown perpendicular to the ground to create
a level,horizontalplane between the fixtureand the ground, and have the bulb housed within
the lightfixture.Tree strap downlights may be used to minimize seabird lightattractionunless
turtlesmay be present on the adjacent beach.
ir>
Figure 1-: (a)Wall mount cylinderdown-light,(b)bollardswith downward-directed louvers,and (c)
signlightsangled downward. From
http://mvfwc.com/media/418417/SeaTurtle LiehtingGuidelines.pdf(FWC 2011).
1.5. Place Lights Under Eaves
Lightfixturesplaced under buildingeaves can achievethe functionalequivalentof a fullcut-off
fixture.The architecturaleave acts as shieldto prevent lightfrom shiningdirectlyupward.
1.6.ShiftLightingAccording to the Moon Phase
This minimizationmeasure addresses lightingforwhich the need, or purpose, forthe lighting
can be shiftedintiming each year to coincidewith the moon phase. Because a reduction in
lightattractionhas been correlatedwith the fullphase of the moon (Reed et al.1985; Telferet
al.1987) lightsfor essentialfunctions,and forwhich that function can be shiftedintiming,
should coincidewith the fullphase of the moon and avoid the dark phase of the moon. Itis
important to note that a fullmoon that isobscured by heavy cloud cover could simulate the
dark phase of the moon. By not activatingthose lightsduringthe dark phase of the moon the
effectof those lightsisreduced. Examples of activitiesthat could be minimized with this
measure includescheduling of nighttime events,such as festivalsor sportingevents.
1.7.InstallMotion Sensors for Motion-activated Lighting
Motion sensors switch lightson only when triggered,thereby limitingthe time that the light
stayson and reducingitspotentialforseabirdlightattraction.Ifa sensor lightisrequired for
securitypurposes, the lightequipped with the sensor should be at low lightlevels.For
example. LightEmittingDiode (LED) streetlightsand parking lotlightscan be activated when
needed and dim when no activityisdetected nearby. However for those fixtures,fullcut-off
designs or the functionalequivalents are recommended because of the possibilityof light
attractionoccurringwhen the motion-sensor lightisactivated or inthe event that the motion
sensor equipment malfunctions and the lightremains on.
Where motion sensors are impractical(eg at sportingevents),stadium lightsshould be turned
offas soon as the publicleavesthe stadium.
1.8.Decrease LightingLevels
Thismeasure addressesloweringlightintensitylevels(e.g.,measured inlumens) while still
meeting the need to safelycomplete tasksand servethe purpose of the light.Guidance on
standardsforthe appropriatelightinglevelfora particularlightfunctionshould be followed as
provided by the appropriateagency or professionaland technicalorganization. For example
the IlluminatingEngineeringSocietyof North America (lESNA)providesrecommendations for
lightlevelsforseveralapplicationsincludingparkinglots,walkways, and roads. Inaddition
individualentitiesmay have standardsand best practicesfor lightingneeds.
For many applicationswhere lightingIsneeded, brighterlightingmay not always provide the
best lightingforthe needed function.Itisoftenthe case where reduced lightinglevelscan
provide forthe needed functionof the lighting.For example, for securitypurposes overly
brightlightstend to createblindspots,or very dark shadows, outsidethe litarea that preclude
effectivevisibility.Well placed,but reduced lightingcan providefor more effectivesecurity.
Therefore,when Participantsseek to enhance onsitevisibilityforsecurity,while reducing riskto
seabirds,the appropriatereductionof lightlevels(alongwith shieldingand re-anglinglights)
forms a startingpointto accomplish both purposes.
1.9.Decrease Visibilityof InteriorLights
Facilitieswith largeand/or numerous windows, tallbuildingprofiles,or largeglassfacades may
alsopose a riskof lightattractionto Covered Seabirdson Kaua'i.The followingmeasures are
based,inpart,on effortsincitiesinCanada and the mainland USA to decrease harmful effects
of buildingson birdsand applyto seabirdsinthatthey can decrease the amount of light
escaping from withinbuildings(Cityof Toronto 2007; Evans Ogden 2002):
Installscreensor shades over largewindows thatare lowered nightlyduringthe fallout
season;
Modify buildingsand decrease or eliminatelightglow from withina facility;
Create glassopacityto prevent the escape of internallight.Tinted glassor filmwith a
visiblelighttransmittance value of 45 percent or lessshould be appliedto allwindows
and doors withinlineof sightofthe beach;
Installphysicalscreens outsidea building;
Installlandscapinginfrontof largewindows;
Closeallwindow blindsafterdaylighthours untilsunrise;
Stagger the operation of lightsinthe evening or morning hours so that not aillightsare
turned on at once; and
Maximize the number of offices or indoor rooms that turn offalllightsaftersunset;
● Placeremindernoticeson switchestoturnout lightsor draw curtains/blindsin
oceanfront rooms. This should include coastal areas that are on the perpendicularsides
of the structure;
Turn offroom and lanailightingthatare not needed;
Relocatemoveable lamps away from windows thatare visiblefrom the beach;
a.
b.
and
Close opaque curtainsor blindsafterdark to block insidelightfrom shining
outside.
c.
1.10.Use Light>iessTechnologies
Where conditionsand facilityneeds permit technologiesthatdo not use lightsuch as closed-
circuittelevision(CCT) with infraredilluminators,may be effectivelyemployed to "see"atnight
thus enabling some of the lightsto be turned off.For example, any fenced areas or the dark
sides of facilitiescan be monitored with CCT so that lightsdo not need to be used or Installed.
1.11.PlantVegetation Around Lightsto Reduce LightVisibility
Trees and shrubs can be planted so that they over-arch lightsor shieldsidevisibilityof lights
along the coast or along a ridge,for example. Whether the lightsare mounted on 20-footpoles,
walkways, or withinlandscapedareas,having adjacentor overarchingvegetationwould further
reduce the riskofseabirdlightattractionthatany residuallightscattermay pose. Long-term
planningand maintenance of screeningvegetationisencouraged, where appropriateto the
uses and needs of the affectedlights.
1.12.Lower Height of Lights
Lightthat islow inheighthas potentialto reduce the effectof lightattractionbecause lower
lightsmay be lessvisibleto passingseabirds.Installingground-levellighting,such as along
walkways, and reducingpole heightcan decrease lightwaste and trespass.
1.13.Use Longer LightWavelengths
Incoastalareas,use of acceptable lightssuch as:LPS 18w, 35w, red,orange or amber LEDs
(truered,orange or amber diodes,but not filters),true red neon, and other lightingsources
that produce lightwavelengths of 560 nm or longer(WItheringtonet al.2014).Long
wavelength lights,e.g.,those that produce lightthat measures greaterthan 560 nanometers on
a spectroscope, are required for allconstructionvisiblefrom and adjacentto sea turtlenesting
beaches.Turtlesare most sensitiveto shortwavelengths of light,probablybecause they livein
a marine environment that filtersout long wavelengths. Green turtlesare leastattracted to
longerwavelength lightinthe yellow-orangeto red end of the spectrum (630 to 700 nm)
(WItheringtonand Martin2000).Inthe absenceofotherlightsources,however, turtlesmay
stillbe attractedto longwavelength light.
Filtersdesignedto excludetransmissionofshortwavelengths(<570nm) can be fittedto high
pressuresodium (HPS)vapor lights.Such filtershave been found to be effectiveat avoiding
disruptionof nestingfemales (Salmon, 2006) but even filteredHPS lighthas been found to
attracthatchlings,althoughnot asstronglyas unfilteredHPS lights(Sellaet al,2006). Filtering
alone isthus not sufficientto avoid attraction and disruptionof hatchlingorientation.Bright
white lightfixtures,such as metal halide,halogen,fluorescent,mercury vapor and incandescent
lamps, are not approved forbeachside or shore perpendicularsides of a structure.Limited use
of shorterwavelength lightsmay be approved inareaswhere directand indirectlightor glow
could not possiblybe visiblefrom the beach due to installationof opaque "lightfencing"(see
below).

To County Council Members:
Please vote to keep bike riders as well as cars and pedestrians safe by keeping
bike tours on Haleakala Crater Road, State Route 378, above mile marker 3.0.
I live on Olinda Rd just above the intersection with Makawao Rd, and at the point
where Olinda becomes Baldwin.
The hill is very steep, and both cars as well as bikes race down at very high
speeds ( way above the speed limit). The road has no shoulder, no bike lane, and
is fairly narrow.
In the last few months, during days that I have been at home, two separate bike
accidents from tours have occurred in this area. One required an ambulance. Both
occurred because the riders were going very fast, and in each separate incident,
the rider veered off the road and fell.
Driving down Baldwin there are many turns in the road, no shoulders, no way for
riders to veer off the road and no way for cars to pass safely.
The consequence is long lines of cars piled up behind riders, then cars
attempting to pass in unsafe spots.
Riders, knowing cars are piling up behind them, feel pressured to go faster than
they normally would or can handle safely.
There is no safe way to continue these bike tours on roads such as Baldwin,
Kokomo, Olinda, etc...
Please be proactive, so we do not wait for a fatality to make the change to
regulate the bike tours.
Thank you.
1
Sandra Holt

Date: October 3, 2022
Maui County Council
Resolution 22-206
To:
RE:
Aloha Chairperson Alice Lee and Maui County Council Members,
The Ma'alaea VillageAssociation(MVA) and our 200+ members support Resolution 22-206 to authorize
proceedings in eminent domain for the acquisition of the Ma'alaea Mauka/Pohakea Watershed. This
resolutionpassed the Sept 14, 2022 CARES Committee by unanimous approval.
We commend the Maui County Council and Mayor Michael Victorino for funding the acquisition of the
257 acre Ma’alaea Mauka in the Pohakea Watershed with open space funds. This Isexactly the purpose
for which the open space fund was created.
It is unfortunate that the new owner of these lands has made clear that he isunwillingto sellthe 257
acre parcel to the County. Allreasonable effortsof an amicable sale/purchase agreement appear to have
been exhausted and thisappears to be the only remaining alternative.Therefore, MVA whole-heartedly
supports Resolution 22-206 to initiateeminent domain designation to complete the property acquisition
by the County.
MVA and our predecessor, Ma'alaea Community Association have been involved in effortsto preserve
the 257 acre parcel for decades. The reasons for preserving this land are numerous - ranging from the
priorityof restoring Ma'alaea Bay to preserving the open space and scenic resources to addressing
wildfireand trafficissues at this main access point to West Maui.
In thiseffortwe have partnered with Maui nonprofits includingKiheiCommunity Association,SierraClub
Maul and Maui Nui Marine Resource Council (MNMRC), the Hawaii Land Trust and Trust for Public Land.
We value the commitment of the Dept, of Land & Natural Resources (DNLR) Division of Forestry and
Wildlifeto take ownership and manage these lands to create a "Forest Reserve" with the surrounding
4,000 acres of state conservation lands. This Initiativewill provide Maui County vast resources in
preserving the valuable open space and scenic resources, expand the historicLahaina Pali Trail and
create parks and trailsfor the benefit of Maui's people for years to come. DLNR's commitment of $1
million in Legacy Lands funding toward the purchase demonstrates the value the state puts on
preserving these lands.
It iscriticalthat the entire 257 acre parcel be acquired, and that itbe done promptly within FY23 since
the funding has been approved in that budget.
Please support Resolution 22-206 and move this resolution forward. The public benefits and conservation
reasons for acquiring thisproperty are well-documented and leave littleleftto be said.
Sincerely,
Lyndon Ibele
President, Ma'alaea Village Association
Ma’alaea VillageAssociation
P. 0. Box 2122, Wailuku, HI 96793
maalaeavillageassociation@gmail.com

Aloha Maui County CouncilMember Tamara Paltin
1am emailingyou today to express my sincerefrustrationwithyourcurrentproposedOutdoorLightingOrdinance.

forced to ask you to reconsideryour outdoor lightingordinanceand ask thatyou “tableit”untila fullEconomic Impact

Event industryspecifically,itdoes outlinethe percentage ofvisitorsthatattendLivemusic/stageshows (concerts),luaus
which are traditionallyheldas nighttime events/activities.

Corporate Event industry,butalsothe outdoorentertainment,Luau's,concerts,and destinationweddings industriesas
well.

of Maui County residentsand willdo irreparabledamage toomany smallbusinessesbased righthereon Maui.

companies were forcedto close permanently, and those smallbusinessesthatdidn’tclosetookon EIDL loansinorderto
survive,prayingthatour industrywould make a comeback and enableus tocontinuetooperateand keep ouremployees.
Are you aware ofthe factthatthe Event industryhas a season as well?Well,we do and thishappens prettyconsistently
every year (obviouslynot includingCovid shut down years).Event Season runs as follows:
● CorporateEvent season which runs Jan 4 thruJuly11.
● DestinationWeddings & otherPrivateevents July5 thruDecember 20
● CorporateEvents returnSeptember 1 thruDecember 20
Based on our own small event lightingcompany which specializesinsustainableoutdooreventand stagelighting,80%
of our business isdirectlyrelatedto outdoor event lighting.Our company Epic LightingLLC, currentlyemploys 4 year
round fulltime,2 year round parttime and 6 seasonal full-timeemployees (‘Seasonaldefinedas Jan 1 throughJuly30
and Sept 1 thru Dec 20). Need tmention thatour company members & employees have familiesthatwe support?
1

enough economically on our families?We are strugglingto stayafloatand we battledailythe risingcostof rent,food,gas,

thatyou are not intouch with what the average residentof Maui County isdealingwith.

Aloha Kakou,
I am writinginsupportof our hospitalityand specialeventsindustryand suppliers,ofwhich my company isa
partof.We alltrulywish to malama ainaand malama sea birds,but ina way thatisfairand equitableacross
the board.
This Billwould essentiallyprohibitany and alloutdoorup-lightingand would requireallotherlightingfixturesto be
properly"shielded"to eliminatelightspillagebeyond the horizontalplaneofthe lightsource.Unlikeotherindustries,
theatricallightingmanufacturersdo not offerany environmentally-friendlyremedialsolutionsor retro-fitapparatusthat
would bringlightingfixturesintocompliance. So thisBillistantamount to an outrightban on theatricallightingat all
outdoor evening events at our Maui resortsand event venues. And ifenacted intolaw,thisBillwillhave iBr-reaching
consequences beyond justthe abilityto lightan event space.Without outdoor lighting,therewillbe no outdoor evening
events,and without outdoor events,therewillbe no group or destinationwedding business,which we are ailjust
gettingback to businessafterthe last2.4yearsof pandemic restrictions.
Iflocalsportingand localsocialevents are exempt from the restrictionsinthe Bili,then anyone familiarwith what we do
forour corporatespecialevents would see itas same same. Pleasetake more time to hear us out and offerpossible
compromises or solutions,so we can allimua togetherresponsiblyand equitably.Malama pono!
Me ke aloha pumehana,

Aloha Chair Lee and Councilmembers-
I am writingin support of CR 22-101.
Thank you forthe excellentwork done in the GREAT committee to craftthisbill.
This enablesMaui County toregulatethelocationofbiketoursand unguided
rentalbikes,keepingthem separatedfrom residentialareason roads not built
with bikelanes.Thiswillgreatlyimprove safetyon our upcoimtry roads.
There is a small error in the billand the committee report.The GREAT
committee voted to allow bike tours above the three-mile marker on Crater Road,
not from MM zero to MM three. Please vote to include this correction.
The Kula community has been working to createa saferCraterRoad and
Haleakala Highway sinceformore than fifteenyears.In 2007 community
meetings were held when the community could no longertoleratethe imsafe
conditions when the tours and loose riders were mixed in with residential and
touristtraffic.In 2008 the Kula community asked forCouncilsupporttofund a
study.We participatedinthe 2010 Kimura study.We organizeda working group
inthe Kula Community Associationand Maui BikeAllianceto prioritizetheir
recommendations and met with the Director of Public Works. We have created
billsand testifiednumerous timesoverthelast15yearstoallowforgreatersafety
on these roads, but no Coimcil took action. Due to inaction,Maui has had to
settlewith a woman who isparalyzeddue to a bike accident.
This billallowsbikecompanies to continueto operateaway from the residential
area.On Monday, Isatatthe top ofmy driveway,V2 mile up CraterRoad, at8:10
AM whiletwo fullvisitorbike toursseparatedby eightimescortedvisitorriders
went by beforeI could puU out. Ithen had to followthisstringoftwo vans and
34 riders,frequentlyonly going at 12 mph, forthe nextfevvmilesnot even being
ableto pass in a passingsection,due tobeing blocked by the tours. Six carswere
stacked up behind the tours. The bike companies tellus they regulatetheir
spacing,but theycannot.With thepassageofthisbill,these tours would not be
preventingour residentsfrom gettingtowork,schoolor anything elseand would
preventtheveryunsafesituationswe arefacedwith every day.
Pleasepassthisbill.Pleasegiveour residentsback our roads.
Thank you.

RE: OPDOsition to Bill21. CDl. FDl 12022\ Protecting Wildlife from Outdoor Lighting
Aloha Chair Lee and members of the Council,
The Maui Hotel& LodgingAssociation(MHLA) isthe legislativearm of the visitorindustryforMaui
County.We representover 180 propertyand alliedbusinessmembers and more than 22,000 workers.
MHLA isstronglyopposed to Bill21 initscurrentformat.The Billisnot anythinglikethe HawaiiIsland
Billthat itpurports to be. [Pleasereferto attachment, Hawaii County Code, Article9,Section14-50]
During testimony on September 20, when severalgroups were sharingtheirconcerns about the future
inabilityto have temporary outdoor lightedevents at hotelproperties,we were toldthatevent
companies don'thave any problems adheringto the HawaiiIslandoutdoor lightingordinance.Upon
furtherresearch.Ithas been found thatthe Hawaii IslandOutdoor LightingOrdinance,found inHawaii
County Code, Article9,isNOTHING likethe proposed Maui bill.Article9 refersonly to infrastructure-
typelighting.Althoughitspecificallystatesthatit'snot limitedto the categoriesof lightslisted,the
lightingfixturesmentioned addressonlyInfrastructurelighting.Hence, the contextof the Code Isabout
restrictinginfrastructurelighting.Additionally,there isno specificmention of temporary events,nor Is
thereany mention ofwhere theycan and cannot be held.Temporary events are held at locationsacross
Hawaii islandwithout breakinglaws. Thisisas itshould be.They are temporary eventsalongwith
temporary stages,lighting,seating,and tents,and as such,they should not have to comply with
permanent lightingordinances.
MHLA isaskingforthe Maui Billto be statedmore simply,as isthe Hawaii IslandOutdoor LightingCode,
and with the removal of lightingrestrictionsforalltemporary events.The layersof exemptions and
exceptionswillmake ithard for businessesto Interpretand comply with Bill21 initscurrentformat.
Additionally,enforcement of such an ambiguous billwillbe even more difficult.
Thank you forthe opportunity to testify.
Lisa Paulson
ExecutiveDirector,Maui Hotel & Lodging Association

Hawai‘i County Code§ 14-50
Article 9. Outdoor Lighting.
Applicability and scope of article,
(a) This articleshallapply to the instaUation of alloutdoor lightingfixtureswithin the
County,
(b) The provisions of this article,including provisions for the imposition upon any
person ofthe penaltiesby fineforany violationofthisarticle,shallnot be
construed toexclude the operationofapplicableStatestatutesor other County
ordinances.In the case of conflictwith other County ordinances, the stricter
ordinance shall apply.
(1988, ord 88-122, sec 3.)
Section 14-50.
Section 14-51.
(a) As used in this article,unless the context clearlyindicates otherwise:
“Outdoor lightingfixture”means any outdoor artificialfightingdevice,fixture,
lamp, or other similar device,permanently installedor portable,which is
intended to provide illuminationforeithervisibilityor decorativeeffects.Such
device shallinclude,but not be limitedto,search,spot,and floodfightingused
Definitions.
(1)
for:
(A) Buildings and structures;
(B) Recreational facilities;
(C) Parking lots;
(D) Landscape fighting;
(E) Business and advertising signs;
(F) Roadways;
(G) Walkways.
“Class I fighting”means alloutdoor lightingused for,but not limited to,
outdoor salesand eatingareas,assembly or repairareas,advertisingor
business signs,recreationalfacilities,and other similarapplicationsin which
colorrendition is important.
“Class IIfighting”means alloutdoor fightingused for,but not limitedto,
illumination for walkways, roadways, equipment yards, parking lots,outdoor
security,and other similarapplicationsin which general illuminationof the
grounds is the primary concern.
“Class IIIfighting”means any outdoor fightingused fordecorativeeffects.It
includes,but isnot limitedto,waterfalland pond fightingand architectural
highlightingforbuildingsand landscapes.
"Building official”means the directorof public works or the director’s
designated representative.
“Individual”means any privateindividual,governmental entity,tenant,
lessee,owner, or any commercial entityincluding,but not limitedto,
companies, partnerships, jointventures, or corporations.

Section 14-54. Submission of plans,
(a) All outdoor lightingfixturesshall be installedin conformance with the provisionsof
this article and those of the electrical code of the County as applicableand subject
to the appropriate permit and inspection requirements thereof.The applicant for

fixturesshallsubmit to the building officialproof that the proposed work will

(1) The locationof the sitewhere the outdoor lightfixtureswillbe installed;
(2) Plans indicatingthe type(s)of outdoor Ught fixturesto be used and their
locationon the premises;

manufacturer’s catalogcuts and drawings,
(b) The plans and descriptionsrequired by subsection (a)sufficientlycomplete to
enable the building officialto readilydetermine whether compliance with the
requirements of thisarticlewillbe secured.Ifsuch plans and descriptionscannot
enable thisready determination, by reason of the nature or configurationof the
devices or fixturesproposed, the applicant shallbe requiredtosubmit furtherproof
of compliance. Furthermore, any design,material,or method of installationnot
specificallyforbidden by thisarticlemay be used, provided any such alternatehas
firstbeen approved by the buildingofficial.The buildingofficialmay approve any
such proposed alternate provided:
(1) Itisat leastapproximately equivalenttothe applicablespecificrequirements
of this article;and
(2) It isotherwise satisfactoryand complies with the intent of this article.

Hawai‘i County Code§ 14-55.1
Section 14-55.1. Penalty.
Any person violatingany provisionofthisarticleshall,upon conviction,be
punished by a finenot to exceed $500. Such person shallbe deemed guiltyof a separate
offenseforeach and every day any violationofthisarticleiscommitted. Furthermore,
payment of such a fineshallnot relievethe individualfiromthe responsibilityof
correctingthe violativecondition,nor shallitpreclude the County firominstitutingany
action for its removal.
(1988, ord 88-122, sec 3.)
Article 10. Exceptional Trees.
Section 14-56.
In accordance with section 58-2, Hawai‘i Revised Statutes,to safeguard exceptional
trees firom destruction due to land development, the County desire^to enact protective
regulationsto preserveexceptionaltreeswithin the County.
(1984, ord 84-22, sec 1.)
Intent.
Section 14-57.
For purposes ofthisarticle,“exceptionaltrees”means a tree or grove of treeswith
historicor culturalvalue,or which by reason ofitsage,rarity,location,size,aesthetic
quality,or endemic status has been designated by the council as worthy of preservation.
The term exceptionaltreesdoes not apply to treesplanted forcommercial forestry
operations.Exceptional trees may be designated generally by biota^^ or individuallyby
location or class.
(1984,ord 84-22, sec 1.)
Definitions.
Section 14-58. Arborist advisory committee.
There shallbe an arboristadvisory committee consistingof sixmembers who shall
be appointed by the mayor. The committee shallinclude the following:the planning
director,or the director’sdesignee;one member who shallbe activelyemployed in the
practiceof landscape architecture;and four other members selectedon the basis of
active participationin programs of community beautification,or research or
organizationin the ecologicalsciences,includingethnobotany, or Hawaiiana.
(1984,ord 84-22, sec 1;am 1992, ord 92-12,sec 1.)
Section 14-59.
The arboristadvisory committee shallhave the followingpowers and duties:
(a) To research,prepare and recommend to the councilexceptional trees to be
protected by County ordinance or regulation,
(b) To advise property owners relativeto the preservationand enhancement of
exceptional trees,
(c) To recommend to the council appropriate protectiveordinance, regulations and
procedures. !
(d) To review allactions deemed by the council to endanger exceptional trees.
(1984, ord 84-22, sec 1.)
Powers and duties.

RE: Bill21, CDl, FDl (2022),entitled"A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE AMENDING CHAPTER 20.35,MAUI
COUNTY CODE, RELATING TO PROTECTING SEABIRDS FROM OUTDOOR LIGHTING"
While itisnoble to addressthe safetyof God's creatureshere on Maui, your exemption of football
stadium lightingvs outdoor event lightinginmy opinionisnot very wellthought out.
Infact,it'sludicrous.Ifthisbillpasses,you'deffectivelybe shuttingdown the LiveEvent Industryhere
on Maui divertinghundreds of millionsof dollarsinrevenue to the outer islandsand quitepossiblyout
of the state.Additionally,the passingof thisbillwould negativelyimpact many establishedlocal
businesses,workers and theirfamiliesrighthere on Maui.
You'd be desecratingthe livesof many Maui residentsand theirGhana, allunder the guiseof protecting
seabirds.
Are you aware of the amount of luminous fluxbeing generated, reflectedand emitted intothe nightsky
from stadium lightingand how itcurrentlyand over the decades negativelyeffectsour seabirds?That
amount of lightisquitestaggering.
As a long time Makawao resident,1am aware of the lightpollutionbeinggenerated by upcountry high
schoolfootballstadiums.You can see the sky glowingfromKahului. jIcan see the sky above War Memorial Stadium and Kahuluiglowing from Makawao.
Going afteroutdoor evening events seems a littlesuspicious.Have you ever seen an outdoor corporate
event at night?The amount of lightbeingemitted intothe nightsky isnegligiblecompared to your
stadium lightsexemptions,(and the MACC) which makes the passingofyour bill- a littlesuspiciousif
you are infactsenouslyconcerned about "protectingnativeHawaiianseabirdsfrom becoming
disorientedby artificiallight".
Pleasereconsiderthisbilland the impact itwillhave on the livelihoodof many of Maui's residentsand
the localeconomy.
Eitherpass a billto make the skiescompletelydark and expressyour true motives,or pleaserethink
who receivesan exemption and the justification,who does not receiveone and why.
Thank you foryour time.
Respectfullysubmitted -
Frank Rizzo
Proprietor

thrivingfishingvillageand thevisionto bringlocalfamiliesback to the area isheartwarming.Maui'slocalresidentsneed
housingand the lackof inventoryIsa largecontributingfactorpreventingthat.Yet itseems so many proposed
workforcehousingprojectsare killedby specialinterestopposition.Iquestionwhether the County seizingthe landand
keepingitas open space isour bestoptionto addressany ofthestatedcurrentissues'(runoff,brushfiresand lackof
housingInventory)? i

projectwould be a continuation of theireffortsbut were blockedfordecades by oppositionwith theirown interestsin
mind. Open space by the County would stillleaveus at riskformajor brushfires.The takingdoes not address how the
County proposes to address stormwater issuesnor does Itworktowardsaddressingo,urhousinginventorychallenges.

Council'sproposed Resolutionto the takingof propertyinMaalaea. The new owners are motivated and committed to
working with the County and the Stateto successfullyfixthe stormwater issueslong-termand work towards helping

TESTIMONY SUPPORTING MAUI COUNTY COUNCIL RESOLUTION 22-206 AS PRESENTED
IN COUNTY COMMUNICATIONS # 22-98 "AUTHORIZING PROCEEDINGS IN EMINENT
DOMAIN FOR THE ACQUISITION OF APPROXIMATELY 257 ACRES AT MA'ALAEA
MAUKA/POHAKEA WATERSHED, MAUI, HAWAII FOR PRESERVATION
Dear Honorable Chair and Committee Members,
My name IsTapani Vuori and Istronglysupport Resolution22-206.
Excessive sedimentation and excessive nutrients are the number 1 and 2 reasons for near shore marine eco
system degradation.Both ofthese conditionshave been present in Ma'alaea for decades and as a resultour
embayment isclassifiedas a 303d, impaired body ofwater, by DOH/EPA forspecificallyforthese two
Figure1 GxUch FacingMakai
RoadWailuku.Hawai'i96793.maoioce^92
● 70.7000
reasons.CoralReefcoverage Inthe Bay isestimatedlessthan 8% when in1975 itwas estimatedto be +75%
and Limu has become much harder to find. I wanted to specificallyshare these photos withyou allso you can
actuallysee the damage with your own eyes;words and datawillgo onlysofarand oftenfailtotouch uslike
photos can.
Firstfour photos show the damage on landfrom one gulchoutofseveralon thisparticularland(TMK: (2)3-6-
001:018).Hawaii LegacyLand Commissioners visitedthesiteinMarch 2022 and witnessedfirsthand the
condition of the land and saw how deep the gulches were; 30'+ inthisparticulargulch.Figure4 shows the
largestorm drainIngressalmostcompletelyblockedwithdebrisand earth.
Figure3 Gulch Facing Mauka BFigure2 Gulch FacingMauka A
Figure4 Gulch FacingMakai attheStorm Drain Ingres#
The remainingfourphotos show what happens downstream when there isa storm event impacting the
Ma'alaea Harbor and the Bay.Thisparticularstorm event happened inDecember of 2018.1 have been
involvedwith Ma'alaea community since2002 and Ihave witnessed many of these events over that time span.
To me personallyitseems likethe severityof these brown out conditionshave increased over the years.

TESTIMONY SUPPORTING BILL 21 CD2, FD2 PROTECTING WILDLIFE FROM
OUTDOOR LIGHTING AND PRESERVING DARK SKIES
Dear Honorable Chair and Committee Members,
Istronglysupport Bill21, CD2, FD2.
1am a Board member atMa'alaea TriangleAssociation(MTA) which representsallthe
commercial businessinthe Ma’alaeaTrianglecommercial area. We have a parking lotthat
contains756 parkingstallsand 27 lightpoles most being 30'high.These lightpoleswere
Installedabout 25 years ago when the commercial area was developed and are end of lifewith
outdated lightingtechnologythatisnot energy efficientand not very seabird friendly.We have
now contractedwith a lightingmanufacturer that isable to deliverto our specifications;< 2%
bluelightcontent,< 3,000K,and shieldedlightfixtures.This technology meeting the above
specificationsisreadilyavailable.They are completelyPV + battery operated. Our new lights
willbe 18'tail.We expectto receivethe lightinghardware by the end ofQ4,2022 and install
them by the end of Ql, 2023.
!wanted to share thisprojectwith Maui County Councilconsidering thisIssueas here we have
a privateorganizationthat recognizesthe Importance of thisissueand ismaking the decision
on itsown to lead with a solutionthat isnot only seabirdand sea turtlefriendlybut alsomost
energy efficientand itishappening now. The astronomers willalsoappreciate more clarityin
the nightskies.Iurgethe Maul County Counciltocontinue to be forward looking and continue
to be the agentforpositivechange inand forour Community. Thank you for your time and
consideration.
Aloha,
Tapani Vuori
c.808.561.2022

Re: Maui Council Bill21 relatedto Seabirdsand Bio-Diversity
Good morning.
Iam writingto you as a concerned businessowner of one of the largestDestinationManagement Companies in
the State.The proposed billwillbe devastatingforthe islandof Maui and willdiscouragelargecorporateclients
from holdingtheirevents on Maui.
Pleaseallowme to sharethe followinginformationforyour consideration:
My company has handled Salesforce,ServiceNow, and SAP formany years in additionto many other Fortune
100 and 500 companies. The three companies mentioned are annual customers to Maui who operate large
programs (500+ attendees and inthe case of SAP, approximately5,000 guests buying out 6 hotels in Wailea).
When these programs selectMaui as theirdestination,they look formultiplethingsincludingease of travel,
number of airlineseats,qualityand sizeof hotels,activityopportunities,as well as festiveevening events for
theirattendees.The abilityto hostevents outsideishuge and can be as simple as an oceanfront welcome party
or luauor a concertwiththe likesof KatyPerryor Bruno Mars on stage.These customers do not want to be ina
ballroomor an enclosedfacility- they can go to Detroitand do this.These events allrequireadequate lighting.
We alreadyhave many rulesand regulationsthataren'tcurrentlyimposed in other competitive destinations
such as Mexico and the Caribbean thatwe battleagainst.Having justone more reason forcompanies to move
their events to these destinations will have serious impact on our economy.
Inclosing,ifthisbillpasses,much of the highend corporate and incentivebusinesswillfindother destinations
that are easier to do business. Can Maui afford this kind of economic impact? We understand thatthere might
be times ofyearwhere we modify our lightingdesigns.However, placinga ban on outdoor lightingthatenhances
Maui's alreadybeautifulvenues makes no sense.We have allworked hard to rebuildtourism post Covid and If
thisbillispassed, itwillbe devastatingto an alreadyfragileeconomy.
Sincerely,
Debbie Weil-Manuma
President
